*
* 'flatfile.html' contains Vdbench generated information in a column by column ASCII format. 
* The first line in the file contains a one word 'column header name'; the rest of the file 
* contains data that belongs to each column. The objective of this file format is to allow 
* easy transfer of information to a spreadsheet and therefore the creation of performance 
* charts different from the performance charts that can be created by Sun StorageTek Workload 
* Analysis Tool (Swat) available for download from Sun.
* See also 'Selective flatfile parsing' in the documentation. 
*
* Run             : Name of run from RD=
* Interval        : Reporting interval number
* reqrate         : Requested FWD rate
* rate            : Requested operations per second
* resp            : Requested operations response time
* MB/sec          : Megabytes per second (MB=1024*1024)
* Read_rate       : Reads per second
* Read_resp       : Read response time
* Write_rate      : Writes per second
* Write_resp      : Write response time
* MB_read         : Megabytes read per second
* MB_write        : Megabytes written per second
* Xfersize        : Average transfer size
* Mkdir_rate      : Mkdirs per second
* Mkdir_resp      : Mkdir response time
* Rmdir_rate      : Rmdirs per second
* Rmdir_resp      : Rmdir response time
* Create_rate     : Creates per second
* Create_resp     : Create response time
* Open_rate       : Opens per second
* Open_resp       : Open response time
* Close_rate      : Closes per second
* Close_resp      : Close response time
* Delete_rate     : Deletes per second
* Delete_resp     : Delete response time
* Getattr_rate    : Getattrs per second
* Getattr_resp    : Getattr response time
* Setattr_rate    : Setattrs per second
* Setattr_resp    : Setattr response time
* Copy_rate       : Copies per second
* Copy_resp       : Copy response time
* Move_rate       : Moves per second
* Move_resp       : Move response time
* compratio       : Requested compression ratio
* dedupratio      : Requested dedup ratio
* ks_rate         : kstat: i/o rate
* ks_resp         : kstat: response time
* ks_wait         : kstat: host wait time
* ks_svct         : kstat: service time
* ks_mb           : kstat: megabytes per second (MB=1024*1024)
* ks_read%        : kstat: read percentage
* ks_busy%        : kstat: busy percentage
* ks_avwait       : kstat: #i/o's waiting in host
* ks_avact        : kstat: #i/o's active
* ks_bytes        : kstat: average transfer size
* cpu_used        : kstat: cpu% user+sys
* cpu_user        : kstat: cpu% user
* cpu_kernel      : kstat: cpu% sys 
* cpu_wait        : kstat: cpu% wait
* cpu_idle        : kstat: cpu% idle
* 'n/a'           : Data not available, or conflicting data. eg. multiple different xfersize parameters used.
*
